<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial-BoldMT,Arial" 
align=center><B>CONSOLIDATED STATEMENTS OF CASH FLOWS</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial-BoldMT,Arial" align=center><B>(Expressed
in Canadian Dollars)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial-BoldMT,Arial" 
align=center><B>(Unaudited)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>1.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>NATURE OF OPERATIONS AND GOING CONCERN</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>Golden Goliath Resources Ltd. (the &#147;Company&#148;) was 
incorporated on June 12, 1996 under the Business Corporations Act of British 
Columbia, Canada. &nbsp;The Company is a public company listed on the TSX 
Venture Exchange (the &#147;TSX.V&#148;), trading under the symbol 
&#147;GNG&#148;. The address of the Company&#146;s corporate office and 
principal place of business is Suite 711, 675 West Hastings Street, Vancouver, 
British Columbia, Canada. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s principal business activity 
is the acquisition and exploration of resource properties.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company is in the exploration stage and is in the process of 
evaluating its Mexican resource properties and has not yet determined whether 
these properties contain reserves that are economically recoverable. &nbsp;The 
recoverability of amounts shown for exploration and evaluation assets are 
dependent upon the discovery of economically recoverable reserves, confirmation 
of the Company&#146;s interest in the underlying mineral claims, the ability of 
the Company to obtain necessary financing to complete the development of the 
properties and upon future profitable production or proceeds from the 
disposition thereof. &nbsp;Managements&#146; plan in this regard is to secure 
additional funds through future equity financings, which either may not be 
available or may not be available on reasonable terms.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The consolidated interim financial statements have been prepared 
on the basis of accounting principles applicable to a going concern. This 
assumes the Company will operate for the foreseeable future and will be able to 
realize its assets and discharge its liabilities in the normal course of 
operations. Accordingly, they do not give effect to adjustments that would be 
necessary should the Company be unable to continue as a going concern and 
therefore be required to realize its assets and liquidate its liabilities, 
contingent obligations and commitments other than in the normal course of 
business and at amounts different from those in the financial statements. The 
Company has incurred operating losses since inception, has no source of 
operating cash flow, minimal income from short-term investments, and there can 
be no assurances that sufficient funding, including adequate financing, will be 
available to complete the exploration of its mineral properties and to cover 
general and administrative expenses necessary for the maintenance of a public 
company. The ability of the Company to arrange additional financing in the 
future depends in part, on the prevailing capital market conditions and mineral 
property exploration success. These factors cast substantial doubt on the 
Company&#146;s ability to continue as a going concern. Accordingly, the 
financial statements do not give effect to adjustments that would be necessary
should the Company be unable to continue as a going concern and therefore be 
required to realize its assets and liquidate its liabilities, contingent 
obligations and commitments other than in the normal course of business and at 
amounts different from those in the financial statements. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>2.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>BASIS OF PRESENTATION</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:24px; width:48px; 
font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>a)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>Statement of Compliance </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>These consolidated interim financial statements have been prepared
in accordance with International Financial Reporting Standards 
(&#147;IFRS&#148;) as issued by the International Accounting Standards Board 
(&#147;IASB&#148;) which the Company has adopted in its annual consolidated 
financial statements as at and for the year ended August 31, 2012. The 
significant accounting policies presented in this note have been consistently 
applied in each of the years presented.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:24px; width:48.933px; 
font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>b)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48.933px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>Basis of Preparation</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>These consolidated interim financial statements have been prepared
on a historical cost basis except for financial instruments that have been 
measured at fair value. These consolidated interim financial statements have 
also been prepared using the accrual basis of accounting, except for cash flow 
information. &nbsp;In the opinion of management, all adjustments (including 
normal recurring accruals), considered necessary for a fair presentation have 
been included.</P>

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48.933px; padding-right:-30px; text-indent:-

Judgments and Estimates</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The preparation of these consolidated interim financial statements
requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported 
amounts of assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and 
reported amounts of expenses during the reporting period. Actual outcomes could 
differ from these estimates. The consolidated financial statements include 
estimates which, by their nature, are uncertain. The impacts of such estimates 
are pervasive throughout the consolidated financial statements, and may require 
accounting adjustments based on future occurrences. Revisions to accounting 
estimates are recognized in the period in which the estimate is revised and may 
affect both the period of revision and future periods. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>Significant assumptions about the future and other sources of 
estimation uncertainty that management has made at the statement of financial 
position date, that could result in a material adjustment to the carrying 
amounts of assets and liabilities, in the event that actual results differ from 
assumptions made, relate to, but are not limited to, the following: </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-
size:9pt"><I>Intangible Exploration and Evaluation Assets</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:48px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>Management is required to assess impairment in respect of 
intangible exploration and evaluation assets. &nbsp;Note 13 discloses the 
carrying value of such assets. &nbsp;The triggering events for exploration and 
evaluation assets are defined in <I>IFRS 6</I> <I>Exploration and evaluation of 
mineral resources</I> and are as follows:</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:48px; width:72px;

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>the period for which the entity has the right to 
explore in the specific area has expired during the period or will expire in the
near future;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:48px; width:72px;

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>substantive expenditure on further exploration for 
and evaluation of mineral resources in the specific area is neither budgeted nor
planned;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:48px; width:72px;

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>exploration for and evaluation of mineral resources
in the specific area have not led to the discovery of commercially viable 
quantities of mineral resources, and the entity has decided to discontinue such 
activities in the specific area;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; text-indent:48px; width:72px; 
font-family:Symbol; font-size:9pt; float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>sufficient data exists to indicate that, although a
development in the specific area is likely to proceed, the carrying amount of 
the exploration and evaluation asset is unlikely to be recovered in full from 
successful development or by sale.</P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>5.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>EXPLORATION AND EVALUATION ASSETS 
</B>(Continued)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company has an extensive property portfolio of mining 
concessions, acquired mainly through staking, in the Uruachic District of Mexico
covering approximately 10,000 hectares. The Company has various net smelter 
returns on specific claims forming a part of the Company&#146;s properties. The 
net smelter returns range from 1% to 3%, which have buyouts ranging from 
US$250,000 to US$2,000,000.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>In May 2007 and amended April 2011, the Company optioned to 
Comstock Metals Ltd. (&#147;Comstock&#148;) the right to earn up to a 75% and 
60% interest respectively in the Corona and El Chamizal properties in exchange 
for Comstock spending $500,000 and $200,000 on the respective properties before 
February 8, 2014, and issuing 300,000 (300,000 common shares received) and 
150,000 (25,000 common shares received) common shares respectively to the 
Company over a period of two years. In order to keep the option in good 
standing, Comstock paid $50,000 and issued an additional 200,000 common shares 
to the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company has received notice from Comstock that it has spent in
excess of $1,000,000 at Corona and effective April 9, 2013 the Company and 
Comstock entered into a joint venture agreement to further explore the property 
whereby Comstock shall act as the operator. The Company is responsible for 40% 
of all exploration costs going forward.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>Comstock has advised the Company that it will no longer proceed 
with the El Chamizal option and has returned a 100% interest in the property 
back to the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>In December 2011,and as amended January 25, 2012, the Company 
signed an Earn-in and Shareholders Agreement with Agnico-Eagle Mines Limited 
(&#147;Agnico&#148;) for the exploration and development of the Company&#146;s 
Las Bolas/Los Hilos property.&nbsp;Under the terms of the agreement, Agnico has 
the right to earn a 51% interest in the property by spending $5,000,000 on the 
property over a period of 5 years. The first year&#146;s work commitment is a 
firm commitment of $500,000 with expenditure requirements increasing each year 
thereafter. Upon fulfilling the commitments for 51% interest, they will have 
deemed to acquire 71% interest without further consideration.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>In August 2013 Agnico has elected to terminate the agreement.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>During the year ended August 31, 2014, $2,883,086 (2013 - 
$2,178,691) in deferred expenditures related to certain mineral claims were 
written down, mainly related to the Company&#146;s Las Bolas/Los Hilos Property.
&nbsp;A number of smaller claims were written off which the Company will 
continue to hold but which are not viewed as priorities and management does not 
currently intend to conduct any exploration activities on these non core claims 
in the next year.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify><B>Stock Options</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company has a 10% rolling stock option plan for its directors,
officers, employees and consultants to acquire common shares of the Company at a
price determined by the fair market value of the shares at the date of 
grant.&nbsp; The Company&#146;s stock option plan provides for immediate 
vesting, or vesting at the discretion of the Board at the time of the option 
grant and are exercisable for a period of up to 5 years. Stock options granted 
to investor relations&#146; consultants vest over a twelve month period, with 
one quarter of such options vesting in each three month period.</P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>Nature and Purpose of Reserves</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The reserves recorded in equity on the Company&#146;s Statements 
of Financial Position is comprised of &#145;Share-based Payment Reserves&#146; 
and is used to recognize the fair value of stock option grants prior to 
exercise, expiry or cancellation and the fair value of other share-based 
consideration paid at the date of payment.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>8.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-family:Arial; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>LOSS PER SHARE </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company calculates the basic and diluted loss per common share
using the weighted average number of common shares outstanding during each 
period and the diluted loss per share assumes that the outstanding vested stock 
options and share purchase warrants had been exercised at the beginning of the 
year.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>To compute diluted earnings per share, the average number of
shares outstanding is adjusted for the number of all potentially dilutive 
shares. &nbsp;As of May 31, 2015 the Company had a total of nil (August 31, 2014
- 6,750,000) &nbsp;stock options outstanding. &nbsp;As of May 31, 2015 the 
Company also had a total of 11,988,888 warrants outstanding out of which 
1,155,555 were potentially dilutive. &nbsp;Dilutive options and warrants were 
not included in the Company&#146;s loss per common share calculation because the
result was anti-dilutive.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

their short term nature. The Company&#146;s financial instruments are classified
into the following categories:</FONT></P>

<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify><I>Financial Instrument Risk Exposure and Risk Management</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company is exposed in varying degrees to a variety of 
financial instrument related risks. &nbsp;The Board of Directors approves and 
monitors the risk management process. &nbsp;The overall objective of the Board 
is to set policies that seek to reduce risk as far as possible without unduly 
affecting the Company&#146;s competitiveness and flexibility. The types of risk 
exposure and the way in which such exposure is managed is provided as 
follows:</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify><I>Credit Risk</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>Credit risk is the risk that one party to a financial instrument 
will fail to fulfil an obligation and cause the other party to incur a financial
loss. The Company<FONT style="font-family:Times New Roman">&#146;</FONT>s credit
risk to its financial asset is summarized below: </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<TABLE style="margin-top:0px; font-size:10pt" cellpadding=0 cellspacing=0><TR 
height=0 style="font-size:0"><TD width=24 /><TD width=265.8 /><TD 
width=18.867 /><TD width=104 /><TD width=25.133 /><TD width=97.667 /></TR>
<TR><TD style="margin-top:0px" valign=top width=24><P style="margin:0px; 
padding:0px">&nbsp;</P></TD><TD style="margin-top:0px" valign=top width=265.8><P
style="margin:0px; padding:0px">&nbsp;</P></TD><TD style="margin-top:0px; 
border-bottom:1px solid #000000" valign=top width=122.867 colspan=2><P
style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" align=center><B>May 31,

their maximum exposure to credit risk. The Company does not invest in 
asset&#150;backed commercial papers. </P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>FINANCIAL 
INSTRUMENTS </B>(continued)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><I>Liquidity Risk</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Liquidity risk is the risk that the Company will 
encounter difficulties in meeting its financial obligations associated with its 
financial liabilities as they fall due. The Company ensures that there is not 
sufficient capital in order to meet short term business requirements, after 
taking into account the Company&#146;s holdings of cash.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>As of May 31, 2015 the Company does not have 
sufficient cash and highly liquid investment on hand to meet current liabilities
and its expected administrative requirements for the coming year. The Company 
has cash of $5,975 (August 31, 2014 - $105,407), and total liabilities of 
$465,098 (August 31, 2014 - $114,619). Accounts payable and accrued liabilities 
of $465,098 (August 31, 2013 $45,280) are due within three months. Management 
has assessed liquidity risk as high. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><I>Market Risk</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>The significant market risk exposures to which the 
Company is exposed are foreign exchange risk, interest rate risk, and commodity 
price risk. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><I>Foreign Currency Risk</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>The Company has operations in Canada and Mexico 
subject to foreign currency fluctuations. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s operating 
expenses are incurred in Canadian dollars and Mexican pesos, and the fluctuation
of the Canadian dollar in relation to this other currency will have an impact 
upon the profitability of the Company and may also affect the value of the 
Company&#146;s assets and the amount of shareholders&#146; equity. &nbsp;The 
Company has not entered into any agreements or purchased any instruments to 
hedge possible currency risks.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><I>Foreign Currency Risk </I>(Continued)</P>

font-size:9pt" align=justify>Financial assets and liabilities denominated in 
Mexican Pesos and U.S. dollars were as follows:</P>

<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>Based on the above net exposures as at May 31, 
2015, and assuming that all other variables remain constant, a 10% change in the
value of the Mexican peso against the Canadian dollar would result in an 
increase/decrease of approximately $6,000 in the loss from operations. 
&nbsp;Based on the above net exposures as at May 31, 2015, and assuming that all
other variables remain constant, a 10% change in the value of the US dollar 
against the Canadian dollar would result in an increase/decrease of 
approximately $1,100 in the loss from operations.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><I>Interest Rate Risk </I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>As at May 31, 2015, the Company has no significant 
exposure to interest rate risk through its financial instruments.</P>

<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>10.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial,Times New Roman; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>FINANCIAL 
INSTRUMENTS</B> (continued)</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify><I>Interest Rate Risk </I>(Contilued)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial,Times New Roman; 
font-size:9pt" align=justify>The Company's operations are in northern Mexico and
are subject to various levels of political, economic and other risks and 
uncertainties unique to Mexico. These risks and uncertainties may include: 
extreme fluctuations in currency exchange rates; high rates of inflation; labor 
unrest; risks of war or civil unrest; expropriation and nationalization; 
renegotiation or nullification of existing concessions, licenses, permits and 
contracts; illegal mining; corruption; restrictions on foreign exchange and 
repatriation; hostage taking; and changing political conditions and currency 
controls. In addition, the Company may have to comply with multiple and 
potentially &nbsp;conflicting regulations in Canada and Mexico, including export
&nbsp;requirements, taxes, tariffs, import duties and other trade barriers, as 
well as health, safety and environmental requirements. &nbsp;Changes, if any, in
mining or investment policies or shifts in political attitude in Mexico may 
adversely affect the Company's operations. Operations may be affected in varying
degrees by government regulations with &nbsp;respect to matters including 
restrictions on production, price &nbsp;controls, export controls, currency 
controls or restrictions, currency &nbsp;remittance, income and other taxes, 
expropriation of property, foreign &nbsp;investment, maintenance of claims, 
environmental legislation, land &nbsp;use, land claims of local people, water 
use and mine safety. Failure &nbsp;to comply strictly with applicable laws, 
regulations and local practices relating to mineral rights applications and 
tenure could result in loss, reduction or expropriation of entitlements or the 
imposition of additional local or foreign parties as joint venture partners with
carried or other interests.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24.933px; font-family:Arial;
font-size:9pt; float:left"><B>11.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; text-indent:-2px; font-
family:Arial; font-size:9pt" align=justify><B>CAPITAL DISCLOSURES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company was formed for the purpose of acquiring exploration 
and development stage natural resource properties. &nbsp;The directors determine
the Company&#146;s capital structure and make adjustments to it based on funds 
available to the Company, in order to support the acquisition, exploration and 
development of mineral properties. &nbsp;The directors have not established 
quantitative return on capital criteria for capital management.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company is dependent upon external financing to fund future 
exploration programs and its administrative costs. The Company will spend 
existing working capital and raise additional amounts as needed. &nbsp;The 
Company will continue to assess new properties and to seek to acquire an 
interest in additional properties if management feels there is sufficient 
geologic or economic potential provided it has adequate financial resources to 
do so.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The directors review the Company&#146;s capital management 
approach on an ongoing basis and believe that this approach, given the relative 
size of the Company, is reasonable. The Company&#146;s objective when managing 
capital is to safeguard the Company&#146;s ability to continue as a going 
concern.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24.933px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" 
align=justify>The Company considers the items included on the balance sheet in 
shareholders&#146; equity as capital. &nbsp;The Company manages the capital 
structure and makes adjustments to it in the light of changes in economic 
conditions and the risk characteristics of the underlying assets. &nbsp;In order
to maintain or adjust the capital structure, the Company may issue new shares 
through private placements, sell assets to reduce debt or return capital to 
shareholders. &nbsp;There were no changes to the Company&#146;s approach to 
capital management during the year. &nbsp;Neither the Company nor its 
subsidiaries are subject to externally imposed capital requirements.</P>

<HEAD>
<TITLE>Management Discussion and Analysis</TITLE>
<META NAME="author" CONTENT="a">
<META NAME="date" CONTENT="08/06/2015">
</HEAD>
<BODY style="margin-top:0;font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt; 
color:#000000">
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=center><B>Management Discussion and 
Analysis</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=center><B>For</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=center><B>Golden Goliath Resources 
Ltd.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=center><B>For the Quarter ending May
31, 2015</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The following management 
discussion and analysis has been prepared as of July 29, 2015.<B> &nbsp;</B>The 
selected financial information set out below and certain comments which follow 
are based on and derived from the management prepared condensed interim 
consolidated financial statements of Golden Goliath Resources Ltd. (the 
&#147;Company&#148; or &#147;Golden Goliath&#148;) for the third quarter ended 
May 31, 2015 and should be read in conjunction with them. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><B>Forward Looking 
Information</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Certain statements contained
in the following Management&#146;s Discussion and Analysis constitutes forward 
looking statements. &nbsp;Such forward looking statements involve a number of 
known and unknown risks, uncertainties and other factors which may cause the 
actual results, performance or achievements of the Company to be materially 
different from actual future results and achievements expressed or implied by 
such forward looking statements. &nbsp;Readers are cautioned not to place undue 
reliance on these forward looking statements, which speak only as of the date 
the statements were made. &nbsp;Readers are also advised to consider such 
forward looking statements while considering the risks set forth below.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><B>General</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Golden Goliath is a Canadian
listed public company with its shares traded on the TSX Venture Exchange under 
the symbol &#147;GNG&#148; as a Tier 2 company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Golden Goliath is a junior 
exploration company with no revenues from mineral producing operations. 
&nbsp;The Company&#146;s properties are all located in the State of Chihuahua, 
Mexico. &nbsp;Activities include acquiring mineral properties and conducting 
exploration programs. &nbsp;The mineral exploration business is risky and most 
exploration projects will not become mines. &nbsp;The Company may offer to a 
major mining company the opportunity to acquire an interest in a property in 
return for funding by the major mining company, of all or part of the 
exploration and development of the property. &nbsp;For the funding of property 
acquisitions and exploration that the Company conducts, the Company does not use
long term debt. &nbsp;Rather, it depends on the issue of shares from the 
treasury to investors. &nbsp;Such stock issues in turn depend on numerous 
factors, important among which are a positive mineral exploration climate, 
positive stock market conditions, a company&#146;s track record and the 
experience of management.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt"><B>Overall Performance </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>During the quarter ended May
31, 2015 no significant field work was conducted on the Company&#146;s 
properties. Presentations about the Company&#146;s properties as well as field 
tours and discussions about possible options and/or partnerships were conducted.
&nbsp;Cost cutting measures continued company-wide due to market conditions. 
&nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt"><B>Other Properties</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>During the quarter ended May
31, 2015, Golden Goliath personnel conducted site visits by other parties on 
several of the Company&#146;s properties in the Uruachic district. &nbsp;No 
significant new work was conducted on the Company&#146;s other properties.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Results of Operation</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>For the quarter ended May 
31, 2015, the Company incurred a comprehensive loss $1,522,551 compared to 
$135,178 in the prior quarter and a comprehensive loss of $152,431 in the second
quarter of the last fiscal year. &nbsp;The significant differences between these
periods include: </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<A NAME="OLE_LINK1"></A><A NAME="OLE_LINK2"></A><P style="margin-top:0px; 
margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Symbol; font-size:11pt; 
float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-size:11pt" 
align=justify>The most significant difference in the past quarter was the write 
down of mineral property exploration costs of $1,445,003 compared to nil in the 
past quarter and third quarter of last year. &nbsp;However, this is comparable 
to the prior year when the Company wrote down $2,883,086 in mineral property 
exploration costs. &nbsp;The most significant write down was the Company&#146;s 
Las Bolas and Nopalera properties. &nbsp;It should be noted that Company 
continues to hold all the properties despite the fact some were written down. 
&nbsp;Management believes these properties still hold good exploration 
potential.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Symbol; 
font-size:11pt; clear:left; float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-size:11pt" 
align=justify>Consulting fees the past quarter were $23,500 in the past quarter 
compared to $14,209 in the prior year as director fees were accrued for the 
quarter. &nbsp;The Board believed director fees were appropriate due to their 
efforts and increased work load. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Symbol; 
font-size:11pt; clear:left; float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-size:11pt" 
align=justify>Travel costs were nil in the past quarter compared to $3,693 in 
the prior year as the Company continues to minimize costs.</P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Symbol; 
font-size:11pt; clear:left; float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-size:11pt" 
align=justify>Wages and benefits decreased to $53,956 in the past quarter from 
$5,726 in the prior quarter and $54,886 in the third quarter of last year as the
Company reduced the number of employees in Mexico. </P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-2px; width:24px; font-family:Symbol; 
font-size:11pt; clear:left; float:left">&#183;</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-2px; font-size:11pt" 
align=justify>Office and general expenses decreased to $7,237 in the past 
quarter from $25,100 last year as the Company reduced its overhead due to 
difficult market conditions.</P>
<P style="margin:0px; clear:left" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>As of May 31, 2015, deferred
mineral property exploration costs totalled $1,975,304 compared to $3,318,611 at
August 31, 2014. &nbsp;During the nine month period ending May 31, 2015, the 
Company incurred a total of $101,696 in exploration expenditures. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

discontinued operations or extraordinary items on the Company&#146;s financial 
statements during the above mentioned periods. &nbsp;The large increase in 
comprehensive losses in the fourth quarters ended August 31, 2013, 2014 and May 
31, 2015 were a result of property write downs during those quarters of 
$2,178,691, $2,883,086 and $1,445,003, respectively.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:60px; text-indent:-60px; font-size:11pt" 
align=justify><B>Liquidity and Capital Resources</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company has financed its
operations almost exclusively through the sale of its common shares to investors
and will be required to continue to do so for the foreseeable future.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company had working 
capital (deficit) of ($370,039) at May 31, 2015 compared to of $161,225 at 
August 31, 2014. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s cash and short-term investment 
position at February 28, 2015 was $16,074. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>In the third quarter of 
2013, the Company closed a private placement for $1,300,000. &nbsp;The financing
consisted of 14,444,444 units being issued at a price of $0.09 per unit. 
&nbsp;Each unit consisted of one share and three-quarters of one share purchase 
warrant. &nbsp;Each whole warrant is exercisable at $0.12 for a period of three 
years. &nbsp;In addition, the Company issued 1,155,555 finder&#146;s warrants 
exercisable at $0.09 for three years. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt"><B>Capital Resources</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Other than property taxes 
which are approximately $240,000 per year, the Company does not have any capital
resource commitments. &nbsp;</P>

<P style="margin:0px; clear:left"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt"><B>Critical Accounting Estimates</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><I>Exploration and 
Evaluation Assets</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Exploration and evaluation 
expenditures include the costs associated with exploration and evaluation 
activity. Exploration and evaluation expenditures are capitalized as incurred. 
Costs incurred before the Company has obtained the legal rights to explore an 
area are recognized in profit or loss.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Exploration and evaluation 
assets are assessed for impairment if (i) sufficient data exists to determine 
technical feasibility and commercial viability, and (ii) facts and circumstances
suggest that the carrying amount exceeds the recoverable amount.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Once the technical 
feasibility and commercial viability of the extraction of mineral resources in 
an area of interest are demonstrable, which management has determined to be 
indicated by a feasibility study, exploration and evaluation assets attributable
to that area of interest are first tested for impairment and then reclassified 
to mining property and development assets.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Recoverability of the 
carrying amount of any exploration and evaluation assets is dependent on 
successful development and commercial exploitation, or alternatively, sale of 
the respective areas of interest.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>It is management&#146;s 
judgment that none of the Company&#146;s exploration and evaluation assets have 
reached the development stage and as a result are all considered to be 
exploration and evaluation assets. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Although the Company has 
taken steps to verify title to mineral properties in which it has an interest, 
in accordance with industry standards for the current stage of exploration of 
such properties, these procedures do not guarantee the Company&#146;s title. 
Property may be subject to unregistered prior agreements and non-compliance with
regulatory requirements. The Company is not aware of any disputed claims of 
title.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt"><B>Changes in Accounting Policy</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>There were no changes in 
accounting policy in the past quarter.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt"><B>Financial Instruments and Other 
Instruments</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company has not entered 
into any specialized financial agreements to minimize its investment risk, 
currency risk or commodity risk. &nbsp;As of the date hereof, the Company&#146;s
investment in resource properties has full exposure to commodity risk, both 
upside and downside. &nbsp;As the metal prices move so too does the underlying 
value of the Company&#146;s metal projects.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt"><B>Outstanding Share Data</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The authorized share capital
consists of an unlimited number of common shares. &nbsp;As of May 31, 2015 and 
the date hereof, an aggregate of 106,660,889 common shares were issued and 
outstanding. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company has 10,833,333 
share purchase warrants exercisable at $0.12 and 1,155,555 finder&#146;s 
warrants exercisable at $0.09 outstanding as of May 31, 2015 and the date 
hereof.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>As of May 31, 2015, the 
Company had nil incentive stock options outstanding. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><B>D</B><FONT style="font-
size:12pt"><B>isclosure Controls and Procedures</B></FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Disclosure controls and 
procedures (&#147;DC&amp;P&#148;) are intended to provide reasonable assurance 
that information required to be disclosed is recorded, processed, summarized and
reported within the time periods specified by securities regulations and that 
information required to be disclosed is accumulated and communicated to 
management. &nbsp;Internal controls over financial reporting (&#147;ICFR&#148;) 
are intended to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of 
financial reporting and the preparation of financial statements for external 
purpose in accordance with Canadian generally accepted accounting 
principles.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>TSX Venture listed companies
are not required to provide representations in the annual filings relating to 
the establishment and maintenance of DC&amp;P and ICFR, as defined in 
Multinational Instrument 52-109. &nbsp;In particular, the CEO and CFO certifying
officers do not make any representations relating to the establishment and 
maintenance of (a) controls and other procedures designed to provide reasonable 
assurance that information required to be disclosed by the issuer in its annual 
filings, interim filings or other reports filed or submitted under securities 
legislation is recorded, processed, summarized and reported within the time 
periods specified in securities legislation, and (b) a process to provide 
reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the 
preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance with the
issuer&#146;s GAAP. &nbsp;The issuer&#146;s certifying officers are responsible 
for ensuring that processes are in place to provide them with sufficient 
knowledge to support the representations they are making in their certificates 
regarding the absence of misrepresentations and fair disclosure of financial 
information. &nbsp;Investors should be aware that inherent limitation on the 
ability of certifying officers of a venture issuer to design and implement on a 
cost effective basis DC&amp;P and ICFR as defined in Multinational Instrument 
52-109 may result in additional risks to the quality, reliability, transparency 
and timeliness of interim and annual filings and other reports provided under 
securities legislation. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Additional information 
relating to the Company can be found on SEDAR at <FONT
style="color:#0000FF"><U>www.sedar.com</U></FONT> and also on the Company&#146;s
website at <FONT style="color:#0000FF"><U>www.goldengoliath.com</U></FONT>.</P>

<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" align=center><FONT 
style="background-color:#FFFFFF"><B>CERTIFICATION OF INTERIM 
FILINGS</B></FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" align=center><FONT 
style="background-color:#FFFFFF"><B>VENTURE ISSUER BASIC 
CERTIFICATE</B></FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt"><FONT style="background-
color:#FFFFFF">I, J. Paul Sorbara</FONT><FONT style="background-
color:#FFFFFF"><B><I>, Chief Executive Officer of Golden Goliath Resources 
Ltd.,</I></B></FONT><FONT style="background-color:#FFFFFF"> certify the 
following:</FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" align=justify><BR>
<FONT style="background-color:#FFFFFF">1. &nbsp;</FONT><FONT style="background-
color:#FFFFFF"><B><I>Review:</I></B></FONT><FONT style="background-
color:#FFFFFF"> I have reviewed the interim financial report and interim 
MD&amp;A (together the interim filings) of </FONT><FONT style="background-
color:#FFFFFF"><B>Golden Goliath Resources Ltd.</B></FONT><FONT 
style="background-color:#FFFFFF"> (the issuer) for the interim period ended 
</FONT><FONT style="background-color:#FFFFFF"><B><I>May 31, 
2015.</I></B></FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" align=justify><FONT 
style="background-color:#FFFFFF">2. &nbsp;</FONT><FONT style="background-
color:#FFFFFF"><B><I>No misrepresentations:</I></B></FONT><FONT 
style="background-color:#FFFFFF"> Based on my knowledge, having exercised 
reasonable diligence, the interim filings do not contain any untrue statement of
a material fact or omit to state a material fact required to be stated or that 
is necessary to make a statement not misleading in light of the circumstances 
under which it was made, with respect to the period covered by the interim 
filings.</FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt" align=justify><FONT 
style="background-color:#FFFFFF">3. &nbsp;</FONT><FONT style="background-
color:#FFFFFF"><B><I>Fair presentation:</I></B></FONT><FONT style="background-
color:#FFFFFF"> Based on my knowledge, having exercised reasonable diligence, 
the interim financial report together with the other financial information 
included in the interim filings fairly present in all material respects the
financial condition, financial performance and cash flows of the issuer, as for 
the date of and for the periods presented in the interim filings.</FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt"><FONT style="background-
color:#FFFFFF">Date: </FONT><FONT style="background-color:#FFFFFF"><B><I>July 
30, 2015<BR>
</I></B></FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt"><FONT style="background-
color:#FFFFFF"><I>&#148;J. Paul Sorbara&#148;</I></FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial; font-size:9pt"><FONT style="background-
color:#FFFFFF">______________________<BR>
</FONT><FONT style="background-color:#FFFFFF"><B>Chief Executive 
Officer</B></FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:5px; margin-bottom:5px; font-family:Arial" 
align=center><B>NOTE TO READER</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial" align=justify>In contrast to the 
certificate required for non-venture issuers under National Instrument 52-109 
Certification of Disclosure in Issuers' Annual and Interim Filings (NI 52-109), 
this Venture Issuer Basic Certificate does not include representations relating 
to the establishment and maintenance of disclosure controls and procedures 
(DC&amp;P) and internal control over financial reporting (ICFR), as defined in 
NI 52-109. In particular, the certifying officers filing this certificate are 
not making any representations relating to the establishment and maintenance 
of:</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial" align=justify>i)&nbsp;controls and 
other procedures designed to provide reasonable assurance that information 
required to be disclosed by the issuer in its annual filings, interim filings or
other reports filed or submitted under securities legislation is recorded, 
processed, summarized and reported within the time periods specified in 
securities legislation; and</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial" align=justify>ii)&nbsp;a process to 
provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting 
and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance 
with the issuer's GAAP.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial" align=justify>The issuer's certifying 
officers are responsible for ensuring that processes are in place to provide 
them with sufficient knowledge to support the representations they are making in
this certificate.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial" align=justify><FONT style="background-
color:#FFFFFF">Investors should be aware that inherent limitations on the 
ability of certifying officers of a venture issuer to design and implement on a 
cost effective basis DC&amp;P and ICFR as defined in NI 52-109 may result in 
additional risks to the quality, reliability, transparency and timeliness of 
interim and annual filings and other reports provided under securities 
legislation</FONT></P>
<BR></P>

certificate required for non-venture issuers under National Instrument 52-109 
Certification of Disclosure in Issuers' Annual and Interim Filings (NI 52-109),
this Venture Issuer Basic Certificate does not include representations relating 
to the establishment and maintenance of disclosure controls and procedures 
(DC&amp;P) and internal control over financial reporting (ICFR), as defined in 
NI 52-109. In particular, the certifying officers filing this certificate are 
not making any representations relating to the establishment and maintenance 
of:</P>

other procedures designed to provide reasonable assurance that information 
required to be disclosed by the issuer in its annual filings, interim filings or
other reports filed or submitted under securities legislation is recorded, 
processed, summarized and reported within the time periods specified in 
securities legislation; and</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial" align=justify>ii)&nbsp;a process to 
provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting 
and the preparation of financial statements for external purposes in accordance 
with the issuer's GAAP.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px; font-family:Arial" align=justify>The issuer's certifying 
officers are responsible for ensuring that processes are in place to provide
